Sign in with Apple allows your users to sign in to your applications and websites using their Apple ID. <h2>Support for iOS, Android, and the Web</h2>Developers can use the Firebase SDKs for iOS, Android, and the Web to integrate Sign in with Apple in their applications. <p>Firebase also provides <a href=\"https://opensource.google/projects/firebaseui\">FirebaseUI</a>, a customizable drop-in authentication UI that allows developers to easily implement a variety of authentication flows using any of the authentication services supported by Firebase, including Sign in with Apple. <img alt=\"Sign in Apple now available for Firebase Auth\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1600\" data-original-width=\"1235\" id=\"imgHalf\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-CNFr2m_daxM/Xc3csD_fwKI/AAAAAAAAEZ8/duJXVPHaPYU71fFdQfl2L02rUledu3KQwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/FirebaseAuthUIRotatoCropped.png\" /> <h2>Availability</h2><p>Support for Sign in with Apple is available in beta now, and can be integrated in your applications using the latest versions of the Firebase SDKs for iOS, Android, and the web.  <h2>Getting Started</h2>Ready to get started with Sign in with Apple for Firebase Auth? We've updated our documentation, code samples, and quick start guides. </figcaption></figure>    <p>Today we are extremely excited to introduce the Emulator UI to the Firebase community. The Emulator UI is a <strong><em>local</em></strong> web app that allows you to manage <strong><em>local</em></strong> emulators that make up the Firebase Local Emulator Suite.  </p><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--RWJAFRNnAM/Xsa7rh2ksFI/AAAAAAAAEvw/RlVRiDv70ZEdZ3H1XQ_liq3-y3jWzPLhQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Overview2x.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/--RWJAFRNnAM/Xsa7rh2ksFI/AAAAAAAAEvw/RlVRiDv70ZEdZ3H1XQ_liq3-y3jWzPLhQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Overview2x.png\" alt= \"image of Emulator Suite overview\" id=”imgFull” data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"767\" /></a></div></p><p>Last year we released the Emulator Suite to simplify Firebase debugging and development. Until now, the Emulator Suite has only been exposed through the Firebase CLI. Today, the Emulator UI makes it even easier to develop locally with Firebase. </p><h3><strong>Why a local first UI?</strong></h3>  <p>The Emulator UI aims to give you the freedom to develop on Firebase without concerns about billing or breaking a shared environment.  </p><p>Need to create a function that triggers on the creation of a Firestore document? You can write that code, run it locally, and then create a document in the Emulator UI and see the trigger fire. What's better is that you can even see the logs of the local function to help with any debugging or even just to ensure a successful invocation. The goal is to provide you the safety of developing and testing your code without interfering with shared environments, waiting on deploys, or incurring billing costs.  </p><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Nk8E0ir3gf4/Xsa8nNv8A9I/AAAAAAAAEv4/p9UHdkWZNqUz2EHyJ-ovkyIEJ8B03JrhQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/EmulatorSuiteScreenshot.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Nk8E0ir3gf4/Xsa8nNv8A9I/AAAAAAAAEv4/p9UHdkWZNqUz2EHyJ-ovkyIEJ8B03JrhQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/EmulatorSuiteScreenshot.png\" alt= \"screenshot of function that triggers on creation of Firestore document\" id=”imgFull” data-original-width=\"512\" data-original-height=\"277\" /></a></div></p><p>The Emulator Suite doesn't just help with developer productivity, it also aims to help with team productivity as well. Having a local first environment also allows you to onboard new developers to your team without them needing to manage a cloud-connected Firebase project. Just run a few CLI commands and the Emulator Suite is up and running with local instances of Firebase services. </p><h3><strong>Local first development</strong></h3>  <p>One of the biggest goals of the Emulator UI is to provide you with a local first workflow. Firebase has always been an online connected service. Most development required managing multiple projects, usually one for production and several others for prototyping, staging and development. The Emulator UI allows you to shift away from needing the online connected project and lets you start your development workflow with local instances. </p><h3><strong>Features to boost productivity</strong></h3>  <p>The Emulator UI is not an exact copy of the online Firebase console. It's tailored for the functionality you need while developing. Here's just a small list of capabilities of the Emulator UI: </p><ul> <li>Boots up in seconds  <li>Advanced data editing in Firestore and Realtime Database  </li></ul><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ko64TCzvVQ4/Xsa9EDNi5tI/AAAAAAAAEwE/LaqNFC6dV4com0eEc3IR-DC0xRq4XfgOwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/rtdb-filtering.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ko64TCzvVQ4/Xsa9EDNi5tI/AAAAAAAAEwE/LaqNFC6dV4com0eEc3IR-DC0xRq4XfgOwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/rtdb-filtering.gif\" alt= \"gif of advanced data editing in Firestore and Realtime Database\" id=”imgFull” data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"1000\" /></a></div></p><ul> <li>Clear all data in Firestore with just one click! (Well, two clicks.)  </li></ul><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-zMe63ydmgRA/Xsa9eG-ygMI/AAAAAAAAEwM/6Gw-8yhIWdUaUs5ZnF_JUgjNpADSWinhgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/one-click-delete.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-zMe63ydmgRA/Xsa9eG-ygMI/AAAAAAAAEwM/6Gw-8yhIWdUaUs5ZnF_JUgjNpADSWinhgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/one-click-delete.gif\" alt= \"image of clearing data with one-click\" id=”imgFull” data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"1000\" /></a></div></p><ul> <li>Drag and drop JSON uploads in the Realtime Database  </li></ul><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-6xLtjV8rCPw/Xsa9t1ym7FI/AAAAAAAAEwQ/g1xJz4DEqoo_8PxsfQei29vEkYFEfjgCQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/drag-n-drop.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-6xLtjV8rCPw/Xsa9t1ym7FI/AAAAAAAAEwQ/g1xJz4DEqoo_8PxsfQei29vEkYFEfjgCQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/drag-n-drop.gif\" alt= \"image of drag-n-drop JSON uploads\" id=”imgFull” data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"1000\" /></a></div></p><ul> <li>See all local running instances  <li>Advanced searching/filtering of Cloud Function logs (this one you’ve got to see for yourself)  </li></ul><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-cs1y7PGsfPg/Xsa98cA8YyI/AAAAAAAAEwY/qUPxyMBzy3QsRCxvsnMcY1ilIkZkLqIrACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/log-filtering.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-cs1y7PGsfPg/Xsa98cA8YyI/AAAAAAAAEwY/qUPxyMBzy3QsRCxvsnMcY1ilIkZkLqIrACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/log-filtering.gif\" alt= \"image of advanced searching and filtering of Cloud Function logs\" id=”imgFull” data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"1000\" /></a></div></p><ul> <li>Fast-loading data (remember, it's all local!)  <li>Test cross-service functionality (fire a trigger with a UI change)  <li>Instant code reload of Cloud Functions   <li>Instant code reload of Security Rules </li></ul><p>...and there's still more to come! We have plenty of features to simplify development planned for the future. </p><h3><strong>New design for local development</strong></h3>  <p>The emulators were designed to run locally. This means it has a looser set of restrictions on managing your data. We want to provide you the freedom to quickly delete and restore data without having to click through a million prompts. But we also don't want you to confuse a local environment with a production one. We took steps to clarify that you are operating in a local environment. </p><p>The Emulator UI introduces a new color into the Firebase palette. You'll notice as you navigate around, purple is the new primary color for all buttons, hover and selected states, and other primary actions in UI components. Even the favicon is purple! The online Firebase console uses a blue as the main active state color. With just a quick glance you'll be able to see the difference. </p> <p>We also moved the navbar to the top for quick navigation. The Overview page displays the local ports of each instance as a reminder as well. We also provide a link to get your production/managed Firebase project, to help establish you are in a local environment versus a production one. </p><p><em>pssst… </em>If you spend enough time in the Emulator UI, you also might find some new features in the Realtime Database data viewer.  </p><h3><strong>Getting started</strong></h3>  <p>Make sure you update the Firebase CLI to version 8.4.0 and run the following command: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">firebase init</pre>  <p>Select the products you need to initialize. Which means if this is a first time setup, you'll need to set up each Firebase product you need, such as Cloud Functions, Firestore and Realtime Database rules, as well as Hosting sites. Once everything you need is initialized, run the following command: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">firebase emulators:start</pre>  <p>This will start the Emulator UI on <code>localhost:4000</code> by default. Open your browser to that URL and you'll see the Emulator UI up and running. </p><h3><strong>Let us know what you need!</strong></h3>  <p>We are so excited to see the community use the Emulator UI. Our hope is that it boosts your productivity and happiness when working with Firebase. But this is just the first step. We want to know what you are looking for in the Emulator Suite. <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Firebase\">Send us a tweet!</a> We'd love to hear from you. </p><img data-original-height=\"600\" />\"\"/>  </div><figcaption>    <strong><div>Sam Stern</div></strong>      <em>Developer Programs Engineer</em>  </figcaption></figure> <a src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ZVF6MGMGzhk/XnpStE1N1EI/AAAAAAAAEtc/a0GA8nmG2bcnBfuiTG9LiKz-2pqkXAuNQCLcBGAsYHQ/s640/Firebase_KTX.jpg\" alt=\"Firebase banner. Illustration of a laptop screen and KXT extension\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"480\" /></a> <p>We know that Kotlin is the future of Android and that Kotlin developers want clean, idiomatic APIs when they use Firebase in their apps.  For the past year, we've been releasing Firebase Kotlin extension (KTX) libraries alongside our Android Java SDKs to give Kotlin developers the best of both worlds. </p><p><strong>Today, we're happy to announce that these KTX libraries are out of Beta and recommended for all Firebase developers using Kotlin in their Android apps!</strong></p><p>So what does this mean for you? </p><ul> <li>Full <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/reference/kotlin/packages\">reference docs</a> for all of our KTX libraries  <li>Kotlin snippets in our <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/guides\">documentation</a> will now use KTX syntax  <li>Kotlin code in our <a href=\"https://github.com/firebase/quickstart-android\">samples</a> will now use KTX syntax  </li></ul><p>To get started with our KTX libraries, look for the <code>-ktx</code> suffix in the \"Kotlin+KTX\" section of our <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/support/release-notes/android\">available Android libraries</a>.  As an example, let's see what it looks like to set up Remote Config with and without the KTX library. </p><p><strong>app/build.gradle (before)</strong></p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">implementation 'com.google.firebase:firebase-config:19.1.2'</pre>  <p><strong>MainActivity.kt (before)</strong></p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">val remoteConfig = FirebaseRemoteConfig.getInstance()<br /><br />val configSettings = FirebaseRemoteConfigSettings.Builder()<br />        .setMinimumFetchIntervalInSeconds(3600)<br />        .setFetchTimeoutInSeconds(60)<br />        .build()<br />remoteConfig.setConfigSettingsAsync(configSettings)</pre>  <p><strong>app/build.gradle (after)</strong></p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// The -ktx library has a dependency on the firebase-config library<br />implementation 'com.google.firebase:firebase-config-ktx:19.1.2'</pre>  <p><strong>MainActivity.kt (after)</strong></p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// New global \"Firebase\" class<br />val remoteConfig = Firebase.remoteConfig<br /><br />// New settings builder syntax<br />val configSettings = remoteConfigSettings {<br />    minimumFetchIntervalInSeconds = 3600<br />    fetchTimeoutInSeconds = 60<br />}<br />remoteConfig.setConfigSettingsAsync(configSettings)</pre>  <p>And the KTX libraries that we have available today are just the beginning, as we're working hard to add coverage for all Firebase products and add new Kotlin-focused features in the near future! </p><p>We wouldn't have been able to release these KTX libraries without the help of all the Kotlin enthusiasts in the Firebase community.  We'd like to give a special shout out to <a href=\"https://github.com/rosariopfernandes\">Rosário Pereira Fernandes</a> who contributed so much excellent code and documentation to the KTX effort. </p><p>If you have feedback or want to contribute, you can <a href=\"https://github.com/firebase/firebase-android-sdk\">find us on GitHub</a>. </p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~4/9zvkJ2eRNoU\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 27 Mar 2020 16:18:00 +0000","feedId":10592,"bgimg":"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-9Anwf6yuljg/XnOeisJJhSI/AAAAAAAAEsQ/3hFsXU3KmawsUZcHGa_zGDiKZrzIb5olwCLcBGAsYHQ/s320/sam%2Bstern.jpeg","linkMd5":"bc7c71b64082e57271e8f25839618756","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn37@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-58-34-637_57a0a36438c9877a.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":320,"sourceBytes":21217,"destBytes":9196,"author":"Firebase","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-9Anwf6yuljg/XnOeisJJhSI/AAAAAAAAEsQ/3hFsXU3KmawsUZcHGa_zGDiKZrzIb5olwCLcBGAsYHQ/s320/sam%2Bstern.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn37@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-58-34-637_57a0a36438c9877a.webp","https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ZVF6MGMGzhk/XnpStE1N1EI/AAAAAAAAEtc/a0GA8nmG2bcnBfuiTG9LiKz-2pqkXAuNQCLcBGAsYHQ/s640/Firebase_KTX.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn37@2020_3/2020/08/25/00-58-42-154_9f4f933f4a7154c2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~4/9zvkJ2eRNoU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn18@2020_1/2020/08/25/00-58-42-114_cb17d27348e4f4bd.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317114229},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:58:34","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:58:34","title":"Firebase Compatibility with Unity 2020.1 and Later","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~3/wWixEp6CKYA/firebase-compatibility-with-unity-20201.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-XAe_-wD8fRs/XzbOu7yG3XI/AAAAAAAAE8Q/ZXsKyOCaKgYrdH20iNXPv6rlTWLkXg11gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Firebase%2B.jpg\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-XAe_-wD8fRs/XzbOu7yG3XI/AAAAAAAAE8Q/ZXsKyOCaKgYrdH20iNXPv6rlTWLkXg11gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Firebase%2B.jpg\"> <figure class=\"profile\"> <div class=\"profile-picture\">    <img style=\"margin:0;\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Qr_GjsVjC_A/Xza1nzp-ayI/AAAAAAAAE8E/M7vo2W74yY88UDcIoYH-3yrRBgr9v5Q7gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Patrick%2BMartin%2B.webp\" />  </div><figcaption>    <strong><div> Patrick Martin</div></strong>      <em>Developer Advocate</em>  </figcaption></figure> <p>Firebase is committed to building an easy to use and robust backend service for Unity developers. Recent changes in the build system accompanying Unity 2020.1 have caused some of the integrations that the Firebase games team built for Unity to stop functioning correctly. Our team is aware of this, and is working hard to rectify the situation. Until then, we recommend that you continue to use Unity 2019 for the best developer experience. For those of you that are on Unity 2020.1, the rest of this post details the workarounds needed to get things up and running. </p><h1>What happened?</h1>  <p>The Firebase SDK for Unity includes native C++ code and Android specific logic. It also  requires some build time operations for all of its products to function properly. Because of this, we have written a number of tools and custom routines that make strong assumptions about Unity’s build process. These continue to work to simplify integration back to Unity version 5, but in Unity 2020.1 the engine overhauled its build system invalidating our previous assumptions. This means that the mechanism by which <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx\">AndroidX</a> and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/command-line/jetifier\">Jetifier</a> are integrated no longer functions as well as the mechanism by which the information in <code>google-services.json</code> is transmitted to your final Android game. This is required to initialize the Android side of Firebase and to properly hook it up to the Firebase backend. </p><p>Further, components that the Crashlytics SDK requires to function are no longer generated. In the worst case scenario, this manifests in a crash on launch. </p><h1>Can I use Firebase with Unity 2020.1 now?</h1>  <p>Although we recommend sticking with the 2019 branch of Unity for the best experience, Unity’s new build system is very similar to a typical Android Java project. This simplifies the workaround we will highlight below, and will mirror some steps in the <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/android/setup\">getting started with Android guide</a>. </p><p>Note that because you are performing operations that the Firebase SDK would typically handle automatically, you may have to undo any changes when a full fix is rolled out by our team. </p><h2>Getting Firebase Running</h2>  <p>The first fix is to help Firebase find your <code>google-services.json</code> file. Normally the Firebase Unity Plugin would do this automatically, replicating the work of the Google Services plugin Android developers may be familiar with. When you add or update your <code>google-services.json</code> file, the plugin creates a version that Android reads as a “<a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/resources/providing-resources\">resource</a>” at <code>Assets/Plugins/Android/Firebase/res/values/google-services.xml</code>. Typically this would get copied into your final project automatically, but we can do a little manual work to ensure it gets included! </p><p>First generate a custom <code>mainTemplate.gradle</code> and <code>gradleTemplate.properties</code> (which we’ll need in a moment) via <code>Project Settings/Player/Publishing Settings</code> if you haven’t already: </p> <center> <a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aj9qfVQUWwc/XzahoLfIQjI/AAAAAAAAE7o/nJIaH8SXEzIa93kiwyfimWXpBrpqvDeRwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%25281%2529.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img style= \"width: 500px\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aj9qfVQUWwc/XzahoLfIQjI/AAAAAAAAE7o/nJIaH8SXEzIa93kiwyfimWXpBrpqvDeRwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%25281%2529.png\" data-original-width=\"952\" data-original-height=\"897\" alt= image of project settings /></a> </center>  <p>If you’ve disabled EDM4U’s integration or you just want to be extra careful, now is a great time to also force resolve your Android dependencies from <code>Assets/External Dependency Manager/Android Resolver/Force Resolve</code>. This will update <code>mainTemplate.gradle</code> in a manner that still cuts back on most of the work we’ll have to do: </p> <center> <a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-IMO9tfskWVs/Xzah_F-wh4I/AAAAAAAAE7w/aKNluf_GYY4sd8pie_s5gEKowB5OdH6cgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%25282%2529.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img style= \"width:500px\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-IMO9tfskWVs/Xzah_F-wh4I/AAAAAAAAE7w/aKNluf_GYY4sd8pie_s5gEKowB5OdH6cgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%25282%2529.png\" data-original-width=\"758\" data-original-height=\"712\" alt= image of assets settings /></a> </center> <p>Now you need to tell gradle where to find the <code>google-services.xml</code> file by adding this to the very bottom of your <code>mainTemplate.gradle</code>: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">android {<br />    sourceSets {<br />        main {<br />            def unityProjectPath = $/file:///**DIR_UNITYPROJECT**/$.replace(\"\\\\\", \"/\")<br />            res.srcDirs += (unityProjectPath +  '/Assets/Plugins/Android/Firebase/res/values/google-services.xml')<br />        }<br />    }<br />}</pre>  <p>There’s one more fix to get base functionality working in Unity, you’ll see that towards the top of <code>mainTemplate.gradle</code> there are some lines like: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Android Resolver Repos Start<br />([rootProject] + (rootProject.subprojects as List)).each {<br />    ext {<br />        it.setProperty(\"android.useAndroidX\", true)<br />        it.setProperty(\"android.enableJetifier\", true)<br />    }<br />}</pre>  <p>This code used to go through every project in the build and enable AndroidX and Jetifier. Although we could perform a similar modification via gradle, Android developers are generally encouraged to use <code>gradleTemplate.properties</code> - which is supported via Unity’s new build pipeline. </p><p>So if you remembered to generate it earlier in the tutorial, add the following lines to the end of <code>gradleTemplate.properties</code>: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">android.useAndroidX=true<br />android.enableJetifier=true</pre>  <p>At this point, most of Firebase should function. This includes your ability to measure your game’s performance with <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/analytics\">Google Analytics</a>, use that to customize your player’s experience with <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/remote-config\">Remote Config</a>, and  to <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/auth\">Authenticate</a> you user to begin your game’s connection social experience. </p><h2>Crashlytics Support</h2>  <p>Crashlytics needs a little more work to get operational since it has to embed itself a little deeper into the build process. To continue, you will need the <code>baseProjectTemplate.gradle</code> (the “project level gradle file”). You’ll also need <code>launcherTemplate.gradle</code> since we need an “Application” for Crashlytics (<code>mainTemplate.gradle</code> is technically a “Library”): </p> <center> <a href=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-s0Sd14HG8sQ/XzaiaxshPJI/AAAAAAAAE74/EqgcK4cAkeo_Osf_N2cMm9bPVQFQQSe4gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/play%2Bsettings%2B2.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img style=\"width: 500px\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-s0Sd14HG8sQ/XzaiaxshPJI/AAAAAAAAE74/EqgcK4cAkeo_Osf_N2cMm9bPVQFQQSe4gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/play%2Bsettings%2B2.png\" data-original-width=\"512\" data-original-height=\"482\"  alt= image of player settings/></a> </center> <p>There’s no need to Force Resolve dependencies again since EDM4U doesn’t know about these files yet! But you can always do it to be safe (the way I modified <code>mainTemplate.gradle</code> purposely avoids bits of the file that would get updated). </p><p>Now open <code>baseProjectTemplate.gradle</code> and look for something that looks roughly like: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">allprojects {<br />    buildscript {<br />        repositories {**ARTIFACTORYREPOSITORY**<br />            google()<br />            jcenter()<br />        }<br /><br />        dependencies {</pre>  <p>Inside <code>allprojects.buildscript.dependencies</code> (the <code>dependencies {</code> bit in this example), add this code to tell gradle about Crashlytics: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Add the Crashlytics Gradle plugin.<br />classpath 'com.google.firebase:firebase-crashlytics-gradle:2.2.0'</pre>  <p>and this line of code to the very end of <code>launcherTemplate.gradle</code> to add the Crashlytics plugin to your Application: </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Apply the Crashlytics Gradle plugin<br />apply plugin: 'com.google.firebase.crashlytics'</pre>  <h1>Wrap Up</h1>  <p>We are working hard to resolve these issues  as soon as possible so you can go back to building games quickly, easily, and confidently, with Firebase and Unity. To those developers who did upgrade to Unity 2020.1 and encountered issues, we apologize for any confusion or difficulty that this has caused. We would like to reassure you all that there is also active work on some exciting updates that will aid in avoiding similar issues in the future and bring more transparency to this process. </p><p>If these steps don’t work for you, or a specific Firebase library isn’t working after you’ve completed these steps, feel free to join in the conversation <a href=\"https://github.com/firebase/quickstart-unity/issues\">at the Unity GitHub repository</a> or <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/support\">reach out to support</a> and we will be happy to provide further help. </p><h1>Appendix</h1>  <p>For your reference, I’ve included all of my modified files here. Do not copy these files directly, but use them to verify that you’ve made the proper changes in the proper locations: </p><h2>mainTemplate.gradle</h2>     <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// GENERATED BY UNITY. 08:58:34","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:58:34","title":"Everything we announced at the Google for Games Developer Summit this year","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~3/-1OkWGjm5tM/firebase-google-game-developer-event.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-3hvWcbVcK2s/XnfIw9b8oxI/AAAAAAAAEs0/MwsS7Qyve1UIGlAwZyEGin_5u6Dw5t1GACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlegamesthumb.jpg\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-3hvWcbVcK2s/XnfIw9b8oxI/AAAAAAAAEs0/MwsS7Qyve1UIGlAwZyEGin_5u6Dw5t1GACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/googlegamesthumb.jpg\"> <figure class=\"profile\"> <div class=\"profile-picture\">    <img style=\"margin: 0 0 0 0;\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zOkmz8nFFB8/XcMtXcDZhUI/AAAAAAAAEYo/gT-6hWfECj0MKdpnzAQ6glV9bU0cb8cCwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/unnamed.jpg\" />  </div><figcaption>    <strong><div>Todd Kerpelman</div></strong>      <em>Developer Advocate</em>  </figcaption></figure> <p>Hello, game developers! </p><p>Well, this has certainly been a challenging couple of months. We had been looking forward to meeting you in person last week at the Game Developers Conference, sharing some updates, and hearing directly from all of you. But, obviously, plans change, and we're committed to doing whatever it takes to keep everybody safe. Even if it means recording session videos from our kid's bedroom and hoping the cat doesn't wander into the scene. </p><p>Still, our teams have been working hard to ensure you have all the tools and resources you need to build great games. This year at our digital Google for Games Developer Summit (which you can <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLOU2XLYxmsIKArZgMoMHQCSzQm2imLKy4\">find here</a> if you missed it), we announced some new features that will help you spend less time on infrastructure work, and more time on making your game fun and unique. Let's take a look at some of these now, shall we? </p><h2>Cloud Firestore for game developers in open alpha</h2><p><a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/firestore\">Cloud Firestore</a> is our next generation, scalable NoSQL database in the cloud. It offers features that database aficionados love, like multi-region reliability (for five 9s of uptime), atomic transactions, robust offline support, and realtime listeners that let you build some really great gameplay experiences. And we're happy to announce that alpha versions of our SDKs are now available for C++ and Unity developers.</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/NB2VrCD8N3E\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe><p>Cloud Firestore can be used in many different situations. You could use it to simply save your users' game state to the cloud. Or save a shared game state to be viewed by several different clients in a multiplayer game. Use it to post daily challenges or user-generated content that can be easily queried and viewed by millions of clients. Or build a sophisticated caching layer on top of your existing game server, so you can share your latest gameplay data from your role-playing game or collectible card game with millions of clients, without having to worry about them hitting your server directly.</p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-se1maP9B4Mw/XnfKIZM-SAI/AAAAAAAAEs8/UMMES1YihigSI9d-E2M6i9HizPDbOBLoACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/cloudfirestore.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-se1maP9B4Mw/XnfKIZM-SAI/AAAAAAAAEs8/UMMES1YihigSI9d-E2M6i9HizPDbOBLoACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/cloudfirestore.png\" data-original-width=\"1218\" data-original-height=\"773\" alt=\"cloud firestore animation\" /></a><p>Cloud Firestore for C++/Unity is open for anybody to download and use as an open <em>alpha</em> release. This alpha tag means it still has some rough edges here and there. Specifically, the Unity version of the SDK is missing some of the more advanced querying features. And there's a good chance the API will change in the coming months, which means you'll need to change your method names in the future. But we wanted to give you a chance to try it out, see what cool stuff you can build, and let us know how we can make it better. </p><p>And none of this is to say that the Realtime Database is going away -- it's still a great option for many situations. In fact, the Google Doodle team just used it to power the <a href=\"https://firebase.googleblog.com/2020/01/google-loteria-realtime-database.html\">Loteria Google Doodle</a> that ran on the Google homepage in December. But if you're a game developer who's been pining away for all the great new features that Cloud Firestore has available, you can stop all that pining and start building. </p><h2>Improved package management in Unity</h2><p>The Firebase Unity SDKs are now compatible with the Unity Package Manager. This means that in supported versions of Unity, Firebase will be easier to keep up to date and the Firebase plugin will no longer have to be mixed in with the rest of your game’s assets. The process of doing this is automated with an open source tool that used to be known as the Play Services Resolver, but is now known as the External Dependency Manager for Unity, or what we've been calling \"EDM4U\" around the office.</p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/y0x_5dmEq3M\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe><p>Note, of course, that using these tools are completely optional. We know that many of you prefer having manual control over all of your libraries, and if you want to keep managing them yourselves, you're more than welcome.</p><h2>New Analytics reports</h2><p>Our friends over at <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/analytics\">Google Analytics</a> have built a number of new reports that will be of interest to game developers, business analysts, or anybody who wants to grow a successful gaming business.</p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-tOqmT9NIWHc/XnfKtLyxKBI/AAAAAAAAEtA/iI-1WshEcuYUsy6THsJgmfFO8uw1SbkPQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/new%2Banalytics%2Breports.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-tOqmT9NIWHc/XnfKtLyxKBI/AAAAAAAAEtA/iI-1WshEcuYUsy6THsJgmfFO8uw1SbkPQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/new%2Banalytics%2Breports.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"836\" alt=\"Google Analytics dashboard\"/></a><p>They've added new dashboards centered around user acquisition, retention, user engagement, and monetization, along with some new reports and visualizations that you've been asking for, like First-time Buyers, Revenue Heartbeat, User Engagement (in game days), and trending DAU / MAU (a good measure of \"stickiness\"). </p><p>These new reports are available for all Firebase developers if you've <a href=\"https://firebase.googleblog.com/2019/07/firebase-google-analytics-upgrade.html\">linked your Firebase project</a> to a GA account. You'll just need to head on over to the Google Analytics console to see these reports in detail. For more information, be sure to read the <a href=\"https://support.google.com/analytics/answer/9713967\">Games reporting article</a> in the Analytics help center.  </p><h2>New landing page, too!</h2><p>And what better way to celebrate some new launches than with an updated product page on the Firebase website? Head on over to the new <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/games\">Firebase for Games</a> product page to get a better idea of everything Firebase has to offer to the game developer community.  </p><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-MQ5HzIKoCjo/XnfLGcsgwvI/AAAAAAAAEtM/veJ3xtC1Y-QdxR3OjIdt-zYWLd6-y6JuACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/new%2Blanding%2Bpage.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-MQ5HzIKoCjo/XnfLGcsgwvI/AAAAAAAAEtM/veJ3xtC1Y-QdxR3OjIdt-zYWLd6-y6JuACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/new%2Blanding%2Bpage.png\" data-original-width=\"1188\" data-original-height=\"964\" alt=\"new landing page for Firebase for Games\"/></a><p>While we are disappointed that we couldn't spend last week seeing you all in person, we hope that what we've been able to share as part of the online summit has made you a little more interested in adding Firebase into your next new game. We have some <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/games/setup\">documentation</a> and <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=A6du3DUTIPI&feature=emb_title\">videos</a> to help get you started, and can't wait to see what you build next! </p><p>Stay safe, everyone! </p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~4/-1OkWGjm5tM\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" developing with Firebase Hosting even better! </p><p><h2>Server-side analytics with Cloud Logging</h2></p><p>Our new integration with Cloud Logging gives you access to web request logs for your Hosting sites. Cloud Logging, previously known as Stackdriver Logging, makes it easy to view, search, and filter logs. You can learn from where and when you have visits to your site, your site's response statuses, the latency of end user requests, and more. </p><p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-OKZHP7mzl-U/Xz7JTIXDLLI/AAAAAAAAE9I/GpRPVyvCf70w8COWT4-QJf8Ya4UObhqmwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/ReportLogging.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-OKZHP7mzl-U/Xz7JTIXDLLI/AAAAAAAAE9I/GpRPVyvCf70w8COWT4-QJf8Ya4UObhqmwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/ReportLogging.gif\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"1000\" alt=\"Report Logging\"/></a></p><p>To get started, link your Firebase project to Cloud Logging in the <em><a href=\"https://console.firebase.google.com/project/_/settings/integrations/cloudlogging\">Cloud Logging integration card</a></em> in the Firebase console or visit the <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/hosting/web-request-logs-and-metrics\">Hosting docs</a> to learn more. </p><p><h2>Better compression with Brotli</h2></p><p>Hosting will now compress your assets with Brotli encoding. We’ll automatically serve the smallest, best-compressed version of your content, based on what your user's client is able to handle. </p><p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ujXuhw4sh5A/Xz7Lbt-D7XI/AAAAAAAAE9U/hkYWVwjMoPQMpuZyAhNYmDBDZwfHsu36gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/FirebaseBrotli.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ujXuhw4sh5A/Xz7Lbt-D7XI/AAAAAAAAE9U/hkYWVwjMoPQMpuZyAhNYmDBDZwfHsu36gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/FirebaseBrotli.gif\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"1000\" alt=\"Firebase Brotli\" /></a></p><p>Brotli compression gives you a boost in performance because assets are smaller, use less bandwidth, and are delivered more quickly to your end users. This means you’ll have lower bandwidth costs, while your end users will enjoy faster sites. </p><p>The best part? You’ll get this automatically the next time you deploy. <br></p><p><h2>Easier internationalization</h2></p><p>We know it’s important to you to provide a great experience for your users everywhere. Firebase Hosting now supports serving country and language specific content, backed by the power of our global CDN. Previously, the best strategy was to use Cloud Functions to look at the country and/or language code and reply with a redirect as necessary. </p><p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-oDtsRJ5tyd4/Xz7LluPkTTI/AAAAAAAAE9Y/AKXexZt635QKeIBKlE-FydFxbULhWUqfQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/i18n.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-oDtsRJ5tyd4/Xz7LluPkTTI/AAAAAAAAE9Y/AKXexZt635QKeIBKlE-FydFxbULhWUqfQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/i18n.png\" data-original-width=\"814\" data-original-height=\"507\" a;t=\"i18n\" /></a></p><p>Firebase Hosting’s i18n rewrites allow developers to serve different content, depending on a user's language preferences or country location. In your public directory, create an i18n directory containing separate folders for each language/country combination, then add the <code>i18n</code> field to your project's <code>firebase.json</code> config. I18n rewrites also work for localized 404 pages. Learn more about using i18n rewrites in our <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/hosting/i18n-rewrites\">documentation</a>. </p><p><h2>More is in store!</h2></p><p>We hope you all are excited data-original-height=\"600\" />\" />  </div><figcaption>    <strong><div>Shobhit Chugh</div></strong>      <em>Product Manager</em>  </figcaption></figure>  <p>With our announcement of the <a href=\"https://firebase.googleblog.com/2020/02/announcing-firebase-crashlytics-sdk-beta.html\">Firebase Crashlytics SDK Beta</a> in February, we provided a path to help you remove all Fabric dependencies in your code, and complete your migration to Firebase. Since then, tens of thousands of apps have adopted the Beta SDK, and several hundreds of millions of end-users are using apps that include the SDK. Thank you to the adopters of our Beta SDKs; with your help, we have been able to polish and debug our SDK so we could ship it in its best possible launch state. </p><p>We are excited to announce that the Firebase Crashlytics SDK is now publicly available!  Whether your app was migrated from Fabric or created in Firebase, we encourage you to <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/crashlytics/upgrade-sdk\">upgrade to the official version of the Firebase Crashlytics SDK</a>. </p><p>Now that the Firebase Crashlytics SDK is publicly available, we are deprecating the legacy Fabric SDK. The Fabric SDK will continue reporting your app's crashes until November 15, 2020. On this date, the Fabric SDK, and beta versions of the Firebase Crashlytics SDK, will no longer send crashes to your Firebase dashboard. To continue getting crash reports in the Firebase console, make sure your app has the following versions of the Firebase Crashlytics SDK, or newer: 17.0.0+ for Android, 4.0.0+ for iOS, and 6.15.0+ for Unity. Developers new to Crashlytics should begin with our <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/crashlytics/get-started-new-sdk\">getting started docs</a>. </p><p>As always, we’d love to hear your feedback! Let us know what you think through our <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/support\">official support page</a>! </p><p>Happy coding! </p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~4/HctzEAvS7UE\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 09 Jun 2020 16:02:00 +0000","feedId":10592,"bgimg":"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-c_A4kawPTqQ/XkyK50vldMI/AAAAAAAAEqg/tS5wkRQFhwwRiYMIMYJxyCwJzxaugRblACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/shobit.jpg","linkMd5":"366e49e54258b3ce823f9ce5eb527e2e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn22@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-58-34-475_b5a6aade7b25b8a9.webp","destWidth":600,"destHeight":600,"sourceBytes":81615,"destBytes":34666,"author":"Firebase","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-c_A4kawPTqQ/XkyK50vldMI/AAAAAAAAEqg/tS5wkRQFhwwRiYMIMYJxyCwJzxaugRblACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/shobit.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn22@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-58-34-475_b5a6aade7b25b8a9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~4/HctzEAvS7UE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn94@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-58-42-237_435c30e0bee082ce.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317114229},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:58:34","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:58:34","title":" Enhance your TensorFlow Lite deployment with Firebase","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~3/0EBmJi2FRU0/enhance-your-tensorflow-lite-deployment-with-firebase.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-DQof7wFzbis/XvVGlaPztRI/AAAAAAAAE0Q/OToWUKETuL4UViJ2WrlcCKJhDZISgrGwwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/tensorflowandfirebase.png\"><img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-DQof7wFzbis/XvVGlaPztRI/AAAAAAAAE0Q/OToWUKETuL4UViJ2WrlcCKJhDZISgrGwwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/tensorflowandfirebase.png\">  <figure class=\"profile\"> <div class=\"profile-picture\">    <img style=\"margin:0;\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-D81ukuSOrXw/XvVG_PB4GxI/AAAAAAAAE0c/5ee2czf5H5s2NKfjkbiUxARynMq5PyTIACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2020-06-25%2Bat%2B5.53.04%2BPM.png\" />  </div><figcaption>    <strong><div><a href=\"https://twitter.com/khanhlvg\">Khanh LeViet</a></div></strong>      <em>TensorFlow Developer Advocate</em>  </figcaption></figure><br><i>This article originally appeared on the <a href=\"https://blog.tensorflow.org/2020/06/enhance-your-tensorflow-lite-deployment-with-firebase.html\">TensorFlow blog</a>.</i><br><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-DQof7wFzbis/XvVGlaPztRI/AAAAAAAAE0Q/OToWUKETuL4UViJ2WrlcCKJhDZISgrGwwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/tensorflowandfirebase.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-DQof7wFzbis/XvVGlaPztRI/AAAAAAAAE0Q/OToWUKETuL4UViJ2WrlcCKJhDZISgrGwwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/tensorflowandfirebase.png\" data-original-width=\"1024\" data-original-height=\"595\" /></a> <p><a href=\"https://www.tensorflow.org/lite\">TensorFlow Lite</a> is the official framework for running TensorFlow models on mobile and edge devices. It is used in many of Google’s major mobile apps, as well as applications by third-party developers. When deploying TensorFlow Lite models in production, you may come across situations where you need some support features that are not provided out-of-the-box by the framework, such as: </p><ul> <li>over-the-air deployment of TensorFlow Lite models  <li>measure model inference speed in user devices  <li>A/B test multiple model versions in production </li></ul><p>In these cases, instead of building your own solutions, you can leverage Firebase to quickly implement these features in just a few lines of code. </p><p><a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/\">Firebase</a> is the comprehensive app development platform by Google, which provides you infrastructure and libraries to make app development easier for both Android and iOS. <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/ml\">Firebase Machine Learning</a> offers multiple solutions for using machine learning in mobile applications.  </p><p>In this blog post, we show you how to leverage Firebase to enhance your deployment of TensorFlow Lite models in production. We also have codelabs for both <a href=\"https://codelabs.developers.google.com/codelabs/digitclassifier-android/index.html\">Android</a> and <a href=\"https://codelabs.developers.google.com/codelabs/digitclassifier-ios/index.html\">iOS</a> to show you step-by-step of how to integrate the Firebase features into your TensorFlow Lite app. </p><h2>Deploy model over-the-air instantly</h2>  <p>You may want to deploy your machine learning model over-the-air to your users instead of bundling it into your app binary. For example, the machine learning team who builds the model has a different release cycle with the mobile app team and they want to release new models independently with the mobile app release. In another example, you may want to lazy-load machine learning models, to save device storage for users who don’t need the ML-powered feature and reduce your app size for faster download from Play Store and App Store. </p><p>With Firebase Machine Learning, you can deploy models instantly. You can upload your TensorFlow Lite model to Firebase from the Firebase Console.  </p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-R-LYYOeaK7k/XvVH3SASOlI/AAAAAAAAE0o/Dl4UXcTu-Kc95KyrvtpoiGbJ2XxgIOFFgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/machinelearning.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-R-LYYOeaK7k/XvVH3SASOlI/AAAAAAAAE0o/Dl4UXcTu-Kc95KyrvtpoiGbJ2XxgIOFFgCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/machinelearning.png\" data-original-width=\"1239\" data-original-height=\"743\" /></a><p>You can also upload your model to Firebase using the Firebase ML <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/ml/manage-hosted-models\">Model Management API</a>. This is especially useful when you have a machine learning pipeline that automatically retrains models with new data and uploads them directly to Firebase. Here is a code snippet in Python to upload a TensorFlow Lite model to Firebase ML.  </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\"># Load a tflite file and upload it to Cloud Storage.<br />source = ml.TFLiteGCSModelSource.from_tflite_model_file('example.tflite')<br /><br /># Create the model object.<br />tflite_format = ml.TFLiteFormat(tflite_source=source)<br />model = ml.Model(display_name=\"example_model\", model_format=tflite_format)<br /><br /># Add the model to your Firebase project and publish it.<br />new_model = ml.create_model(model)<br />ml.publish_model(new_model.model_id)</pre>  <p>Once your TensorFlow Lite model has been uploaded to Firebase, you can download it in your mobile app at any time and initialize a TensorFlow Lite interpreter with the downloaded model. Here is how you do it on Android. </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">val remoteModel = FirebaseCustomRemoteModel.Builder(\"example_model\").build()<br /><br />// Get the last/cached model file.<br />FirebaseModelManager.getInstance().getLatestModelFile(remoteModel)<br />  .addOnCompleteListener { task -><br />    val modelFile = task.result<br />    if (modelFile != null) {<br />      // Initialize a TF Lite interpreter with the downloaded model.<br />      interpreter = Interpreter(modelFile)<br />    }<br />  }</pre>  <h2>Measure inference speed on user devices</h2>  <p>There is a diverse range of mobile devices available in the market nowadays, from flagship devices with powerful chips optimized to run machine learning models to cheap devices with low-end CPUs. Therefore, your model inference speed on your users’ devices may vary largely across your user base, leaving you wondering if your model is too slow or even unusable for some of your users with low-end devices. </p><p>You can use Performance Monitoring to measure how long your model inference takes across all of your user devices. As it is impractical to have all devices available in the market for testing in advance, the best way to find out about your model performance in production is to directly measure it on user devices. Firebase Performance Monitoring is a general purpose tool for measuring performance of mobile apps, so you also can measure any arbitrary process in your app, such as pre-processing or post-processing code. Here is how you do it on Android. </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">// Initialize a Firebase Performance Monitoring trace<br />val modelInferenceTrace = firebasePerformance.newTrace(\"model_inference\")<br /><br />// Run inference with TensorFlow Lite<br />interpreter.run(...)<br /><br />// End the Firebase Performance Monitoring trace<br />modelInferenceTrace.stop()</pre>  <p>Performance data measured on each user device is uploaded to Firebase server and aggregated to provide a big picture of your model performance across your user base. From the Firebase console, you can easily identify devices that demonstrate slow inference, or see how inference speed differs between OS versions. </p><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-XMutFj1xbb0/XvVICzL7E0I/AAAAAAAAE0s/gwe7n2fMHQc7ErjXU_IbCIf2z6vv45ggQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/inferencespeeds.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-XMutFj1xbb0/XvVICzL7E0I/AAAAAAAAE0s/gwe7n2fMHQc7ErjXU_IbCIf2z6vv45ggQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/inferencespeeds.png\" data-original-width=\"923\" data-original-height=\"828\" /></a> <h2>A/B test multiple model versions</h2>  <p>When you iterate on your machine learning model and come up with an improved model, you may feel very eager to release it to a production right away. However, it is not rare that a model may perform well on test data but fail badly in production. Therefore, the best practice is to roll out your model to a smaller set of users, A/B test it with the original model and closely monitor how it affects your important business metrics before releasing it to all of your users. </p><p>Firebase A/B Testing enables you to run this kind of A/B testing with minimal effort. The steps required are: </p><ol> <li>Upload all TensorFlow Lite model versions that you want to test to Firebase, giving each one a different name.  <li>Setup Firebase Remote Config in the Firebase console to manage the TensorFlow Lite model name used in the app.   <ul>  <li>Update the client app to fetch TensorFlow Lite model name from Remote Config and download the corresponding TensorFlow Lite model from Firebase. </li>  </ul> <li>Setup A/B testing in the Firebase console.  <ul>  <li>Decide the testing plan (e.g. how many percent of your user base to test each model version).   <li>Decide the metric(s) that you want to optimize for (e.g. number of conversions, user retention etc.). </li>  </ul></li>  </ol><p>Here is an example of setting up an A/B test with TensorFlow Lite models. We deliver each of two versions of our model to 50% of our user base and with the goal of optimizing for multiple metrics. </p><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Y7Ql2cCC_9o/XvVINSAFWWI/AAAAAAAAE00/40oEWia7vhggsRKGhjAKbk5eCObooO4VACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/experimentoverview.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Y7Ql2cCC_9o/XvVINSAFWWI/AAAAAAAAE00/40oEWia7vhggsRKGhjAKbk5eCObooO4VACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/experimentoverview.png\" data-original-width=\"902\" data-original-height=\"715\" /></a><p>Then we change our app to fetch the model name from Firebase and use it to download the TensorFlow Lite model assigned to each device. </p>   <pre class=\"prettyprint\">val remoteConfig = Firebase.remoteConfig<br />remoteConfig.fetchAndActivate()<br />  .addOnCompleteListener(this) { task -><br />      // Get the model name from Firebase Remote Config<br />      val modelName = remoteConfig[\"model_name\"].asString()<br />      <br />      // Download the model from Firebase ML<br />      val remoteModel = FirebaseCustomRemoteModel.Builder(modelName).build()<br />      val manager = FirebaseModelManager.getInstance()<br />      manager.download(remoteModel).addOnCompleteListener {<br />        // Initialize a TF Lite interpreter with the downloaded model<br />        interpreter = Interpreter(modelFile)<br />      }<br />  }</pre>  <p>After you have started the A/B test, Firebase will automatically aggregate the metrics on how your users react to different versions of your model and show you which version performs better. Once you are confident with the A/B test result, you can roll out the better version to all of your users with just one click. </p><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-U9xXn0fJ0Zo/XvVIaJBqknI/AAAAAAAAE08/lnmpNLgiiYIYzG9KH60LSbXbwwJJR3a4ACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/clearimprovements.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" ><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-U9xXn0fJ0Zo/XvVIaJBqknI/AAAAAAAAE08/lnmpNLgiiYIYzG9KH60LSbXbwwJJR3a4ACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/clearimprovements.png\" data-original-width=\"953\" data-original-height=\"566\" /></a><h2>Next steps</h2>  <p>Check out this codelab (<a href=\"https://codelabs.developers.google.com/codelabs/digitclassifier-android/index.html\">Android</a> version or <a href=\"https://codelabs.developers.google.com/codelabs/digitclassifier-ios/index.html\">iOS</a> version) to learn step by step how to integrate these Firebase features into your app. It starts with an app that uses a TensorFlow Lite model to recognize handwritten digits and show you: </p><ul> <li>How to upload a TensorFlow Lite model to Firebase via the Firebase Console and the Firebase Model Management API.  <li>How to dynamically download a TensorFlow Lite model from Firebase and use it.  <li>How to measure pre-processing, post processing and inference time on user devices with Firebase Performance Monitoring.  <li>How to A/B test two versions of a handwritten digit classification model with Firebase A/B Testing. </li></ul><h2>Acknowledgements</h2>  <p><i>Amy Jang, Ibrahim Ulukaya, erx27/cdn25@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-58-42-257_4212891d6a9f1880.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598317114228},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25  </div><figcaption>    <strong><div><a href=\"https://twitter.com/cantforget\">Francis Ma</a></div></strong>      <em>Head of Product</em>  </figcaption></figure>  <img border=\"0\" style=\"width:100%\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-bfa2nWeA9js/XxfN7OopbqI/AAAAAAAAE2U/HUk-v-Q86ggiWwq1WX7ODyeZKb4bmi61wCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/pasted%2Bimage%2B0%2B%25283%2529.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"476\" />  <p>Our team is driven by the belief that apps have drastically improved the way we live, work, learn, and socialize, keeping us connected to each other and plugged into the information we need. Now more than ever, we understand the importance of supporting our developer community by ensuring you have the technology and resources you need to keep your business up and running. Whether you’re a high-growth startup or a global enterprise, we’re still here to help you build and operate your app. </p><a name='more'></a><p>While we aren’t able to meet in person, last month we launched <a href=\"http://firebase.google.com/live\">Firebase Live</a>, a month-long web series consisting of talks, tips, and technical tutorials aimed at increasing your <strong>productivity, knowledge, and connectivity</strong>. During Firebase Live, we released 5 videos, 4 codelab walkthrough videos, an interactive demo, tons of product updates, and answered hundreds of questions from the thousands of developers that joined us live. If you missed the online event - or if you simply want a refresher - here’s a recap of everything we announced plus highlights of our recent launches. </p><h2>Firebase tools for boosting productivity </h2>  <p>We know first-hand that when you’re working from home, you face a new set of distractions. With the following Firebase tools, you can accelerate app development, create efficient workflows, and ship your app faster so you remain productive.  </p><h3><strong>Introducing the new emulator UI for local development</strong></h3>  <p>Last year, we launched the <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/emulator-suite\">Firebase Emulator Suite</a> to let you run emulated versions of our backend products for a faster and safer development experience. We heard from you that you also wanted a visual tool that could help you develop locally and do things like filter through logs and test your data structures.  </p><p>That’s why we recently launched the <a href=\"https://firebase.googleblog.com/2020/05/local-firebase-emulator-ui.html\">new local emulator UI</a> into beta, which makes  it possible to run services <em>locally</em> on your machine via a web app with a distinguishable UI. Now, you can develop and test your code in a safe sandbox environment without interfering with shared environments, waiting on deploys, or incurring billing costs. Not only does the emulator UI boost developer productivity with features like advanced data editing and searching, it also increases <em>team</em> productivity because you can onboard new developers with just a handful of CLI commands that create local instances of Firebase services in minutes. By shifting to a local-first developer workflow, you get the freedom to experiment and rapidly iterate, without the fear of breaking anything.  </p><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-1_HnklDBkA8/XxfR3VFUFEI/AAAAAAAAE2o/BdcwwvDORdkuZvQvqMdIHX2pEMvjQQ8CACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/01-%2BEmulator%2BSuite.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-1_HnklDBkA8/XxfR3VFUFEI/AAAAAAAAE2o/BdcwwvDORdkuZvQvqMdIHX2pEMvjQQ8CACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/01-%2BEmulator%2BSuite.png\" data-original-width=\"1309\" data-original-height=\"627\" /></a></div></p><p>You can learn how to set up these emulators to quickly prototype and develop, create better unit and integration tests, and get a walkthrough of the new emulator UI in the below video from Firebase Live. </p><p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/pkgvFNPdiEs\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p><h3><strong>Simplifying the process of writing and testing security rules</strong></h3>  <p>One of the new features of the Emulator Suite is that it supports instant code reload of <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/rules\">security rules</a>, which are the main line of defense between your database and untrustworthy clients. In addition, we’ve recently made <a href=\"https://firebase.googleblog.com/2020/06/new-firestore-security-rules-features.html\">several other improvements</a> to the tools for writing, debugging, and monitoring security rules, including making the rules language itself more expressive, streamlining rule logic, and adding local variables - a highly requested feature now available with functions! </p><p>Traditionally, security rules haven’t been the most straightforward thing to develop or test. Our goal with these updates is to significantly improve this process and make a lot of formerly difficult tasks easier. In the following video from Firebase Live, you can learn how to efficiently unit test your security rules using helpful libraries and the latest Firebase Emulator Suite so you can feel confident that the rules will work as you expect when deployed.  </p><p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/VDulvfBpzZE\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p><strong><h3>Painless user authentication with Sign in with Apple</strong></h3>  <p><strong></strong>Authenticating your users is the first step in giving them a personalized app experience. But building and maintaining your own authentication system can take months. <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/auth\">Firebase Authentication</a> offers you a complete, customizable, end-to-end identity solution that can be set up in under 10 lines of code. It makes it quick and easy to sign in and verify your users using a variety of popular identity providers, including email and password, phone authentication, Facebook, Google, Twitter, and more. During our last release, we added <a href=\"https://firebase.googleblog.com/2019/11/sign-in-with-apple-auth.html\">beta support for Sign in with Apple</a> which allows users to log into your mobile apps, web apps, and games using their Apple ID.  </p><p>On top of updating our<a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/auth/ios/apple\"> comprehensive docs and code samples</a>, we used Firebase Live as an opportunity to create a new video showing you how to implement Sign in with Apple using Firebase Authentication. Check it out below.  </p><p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/BxQsdhglZtE\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p><h3><strong>New Stripe extensions for payment processing</strong></h3>  <p>Since launching <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/extensions\">Extensions</a>, which are pre-packaged bundles of code that automate common tasks in your projects to save you time, at Firebase Summit last year, we’ve received tons of requests for more extensions doing even more useful things. We recently unveiled two brand new extensions built in partnership with our friends at <a href=\"https://stripe.com/\">Stripe</a>. The first one, <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/extensions/firestore-invoice-stripe\">Send Invoices with Stripe,</a> lets you programmatically create and send branded customer invoices using the Stripe payments platform. The second extension, <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/extensions/firestore-stripe-subscriptions\">Run Subscription Payments with Stripe</a>, can be used to create and sync subscriptions for your web users with Stripe, as well as control access to subscription content via Firebase Authentication. You don’t need to learn Stripe’s API or figure out how to integrate Stripe with Firebase, simply install these extensions and you’re ready to go.  </p><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5GhR0KpW7a0/XxfR8eR0q4I/AAAAAAAAE2s/GCUtDEe9yOAXYWI0nvF8pXCEs0IhcF0IQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/02-%2Btypographic%2Binvoice.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5GhR0KpW7a0/XxfR8eR0q4I/AAAAAAAAE2s/GCUtDEe9yOAXYWI0nvF8pXCEs0IhcF0IQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/02-%2Btypographic%2Binvoice.png\" data-original-width=\"1600\" data-original-height=\"900\" /></a></div></p><h3><strong>Enhancing TensorFlow Lite model deployment with Firebase</strong></h3>  <p>We know many of you are looking to, or have already, started adding ML capabilities to your apps. Whether you are starting with an existing <a href=\"https://www.tensorflow.org/lite/models\">TensorFlow Lite model</a> or training your own, you can use <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/ml\">Firebase ML</a> model deployment to distribute models to your users over the air. This reduces initial app installation size, since models are downloaded by the device only when needed, and allows you to A/B test multiple models, evaluate their performance, and update models regularly without having to republish your entire app.  </p><p>We recently released the <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/ml/manage-hosted-models\">ML Model Management API</a> to deploy models programmatically instead of going through the console. This is especially useful when you have a machine learning pipeline that automatically retrains models with new data, since you can now upload the updated models to Firebase programmatically. You can read more on how to <a href=\"https://firebase.googleblog.com/2020/06/enhance-your-tensorflow-lite-deployment-with-firebase.html\">use Firebase to enhance your TensorFlow Lite deployments</a> and try out our new codelabs (<a href=\"https://codelabs.developers.google.com/codelabs/digitclassifier-android/index.html\">Android</a> version or <a href=\"https://codelabs.developers.google.com/codelabs/digitclassifier-ios/index.html\">iOS</a> version) to learn step by step how to deploy and experiment with multiple models. </p><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-gDD7wIm1zLE/XxfSA66drjI/AAAAAAAAE2w/8FYN4jR4SyIAXRE6oy61UxbYF_jjU-gFQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/03-%2BFirebase%2Bscreenshot.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-gDD7wIm1zLE/XxfSA66drjI/AAAAAAAAE2w/8FYN4jR4SyIAXRE6oy61UxbYF_jjU-gFQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/03-%2BFirebase%2Bscreenshot.png\" data-original-width=\"1348\" data-original-height=\"742\" /></a></div></p><h2>Firebase tools to stay connected </h2>  <p>In this era of social distancing and remote work, Firebase can keep you connected to the things that matter most to your business. We want to help you stay attuned to your app’s analytics and performance data, meaningfully adapt your apps’ features and UI to the current climate, and continue to delight users with personalized experiences.  </p><h3><strong>New organizational and targeting tools for your app config</strong></h3>  <p>Changing your app config can be risky and complicated. With <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/remote-config\">Firebase Remote Config</a>, you can dynamically alter the behavior and appearance of your app with confidence - without having to publish a new version of your app. Over the past few months, we’ve been adding new features to Remote Config to give you a greater understanding of your active app configuration and better organizational and targeting tools so you can focus on the parameters you care about most.  </p><p>Earlier this year, we brought information about your A/B tests into the Remote Config panel giving you insight into how currently running experiments are impacting your app configuration. Then, we launched parameter groups, making it easy to classify, change, and delineate key params. These new Remote Config features give teams the power to structure and divide their params in a way that suits their needs, minimizes risk, and makes their app config more manageable.  </p><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cY9PjBpSXgo/XxfSImiHE8I/AAAAAAAAE20/t3OPexX8UgQN9kh8FbuocR3yLfeokYc2gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/04-%2Bremote%2Bconfig.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cY9PjBpSXgo/XxfSImiHE8I/AAAAAAAAE20/t3OPexX8UgQN9kh8FbuocR3yLfeokYc2gCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/04-%2Bremote%2Bconfig.png\" data-original-width=\"1440\" data-original-height=\"789\" /></a></div></p><h3><strong>Introducing Crashlytics BigQuery streaming</strong></h3>  <p>When your app runs into stability issues, you want to be told as soon as possible - even if you’re away from your desk. Now, you can stream your <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/products/crashlytics\">Firebase Crashlytics</a> data into BigQuery for better logging, analysis, and troubleshooting. This is really useful for setting up a realtime alerting infrastructure that notifies members of your team when issues arise. Crashlytics BigQuery streaming enables development teams to automate a lot of the work needed for release monitoring so they can stay on top of stability - no matter where they are. To enable this capability, head over to the Integrations tab within your Project Settings. </p><p><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-4zgVlYvxqLQ/XxfSM6TCH3I/AAAAAAAAE28/vlOYYZBSl2wQUiTacxCIjcgsWf3fF-qygCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/04-crashlytics.gif\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-4zgVlYvxqLQ/XxfSM6TCH3I/AAAAAAAAE28/vlOYYZBSl2wQUiTacxCIjcgsWf3fF-qygCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/04-crashlytics.gif\" data-original-width=\"595\" data-original-height=\"295\" /></a></div></p><h3><strong>Getting the most out of Google Analytics</strong></h3>  <p>If you created your Firebase project after August 2019, your analytics data is available in both Firebase <em>and</em> Google Analytics. What we’ve found is that even though most developers have looked at their analytics data in the Firebase console, not everyone has explored the additional features available in Google Analytics, such as <a href=\"https://support.google.com/analytics/answer/9269518\">comparisons</a>, <a href=\"https://support.google.com/analytics/topic/9266525\">analysis</a>, and closed funnels.  </p><p>That’s why during Firebase Live, we debuted two videos that walk you through <a href=\"https://www.blog.google/products/marketingplatform/analytics/new-way-unify-app-and-website-measurement-google-analytics/\">Google Analytics</a>.  </p><p>In the first video below, you’ll get an overview of the Google Analytics console and learn how to get the most out of its advanced features so you can effectively understand your users and personalize their app experiences. </p><p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/2F2XhgMt8Dg\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p><p>In the second video, created specifically for game developers, you’ll learn how to extract timely insights about player engagement and what can be improved in your gameplay.  </p><p><iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/JDxXiarsrHk\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p><h2>Our commitment to you</h2>  <p>2020 has been a challenging year in many ways, but our commitment to you is unwavering: we will continue to make Firebase a helpful platform that simplifies, speeds up, and scales your app development so you can focus on building and strengthening your business. We wrapped up the first half of the year with Firebase Live, the full playlist for which can be found <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLl-K7zZEsYLnw0-bXz2f9zo6745VQ_2ep\">here</a>. href=\"https://services.google.com/fb/forms/firebasealphaprogram/\">Alpha program</a>. </p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/FirebaseBlog/~4/qdQRpJeqMP8\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\"
